Rightfully so. When I got the diagnosis, I was spinning...  I asked the universe "what are you trying to teach me?" and the answers flooded in & what I received changed my viewpoint. My breast cancer experience turned out to be the best thing that happened to me!! why? It taught me very quickly whats important and whats not in life!! and at an early age!!!!. Im grateful it happened to me young because I had the rest of my life to enjoy the lessons! I often say what good would it have done if I got breast cancer at age 80 and died at age 83 and not be able to change anything! At least I can enjoy the life lessons for 60 yrs and after this experience I changed everything in my life!  Right now, your in it.!!. some days will be good, some days will be low...feel it all.. ups & downs.. surround yourself with positive friends & family...so some great advice I got at the time ... and it helped me was... 1) dont think about whats going to happen in the future.. thats too overwhelming...just think about today only. Live in the moment 2) you mentioned .. you get upset when you think of "what you cant do"... replace those thoughts with what you want to happen....how you want to feel, what you want to be able to do when this is all over.. get excited! 3) finally have a goal... so when you feel low... you know you are working towards something.... like when this is all over ..for ex...."I want to go on a vacation with family to ...???" Good luck, feel it, write it in a journal... (20 yrs from now, you can show your babies how you were feeling and how you got thru it)... Big hug from NY. Vivian :)

I was diagnosed with medulloblastoma at 25; almost 10 years ago. I did the same thing. I had surgery, then proton radiation, then chemo. For me, you have done the worst part. I had a horrible time with proton radiation. Chemo was easier. I was  terrified of chemo after my radiation experience. I lasted almost 8 years without it coming back. I had a second craniotomy. When it came back, there were lots of medical advancements. I'm about to start a clinical trial at the national institute of health, where my original neuro oncologist at MD Anderson went. My oncologist was Marta Penas-Predo and I am still being treated at MD Anderson. Dr. Penas-Prado's specialty is adult medulloblastoma and she is a national expert. Obviously I'm not saying you should change, I have her as backup, and she just started this trial two weeks ago. Take heart. I was in my last year of law school when I was diagnosed, a week before my law school exams and a month before graduation. I was able to graduate and pass the bar. I've been an attorney ever since.

When my niece was 11 she kept complaining of headaches in the mornings after waking up. Her mom and I both told her to go to bed on time and stop staying up all night talking to her friends on her cell phone and her head wouldn't hurt in the mornings. She went to the doctor and the doctor agreed that she wasn't getting enough sleep. My niece saw a segment on mystery diagnosis and was convinced that she had a brain tumor and everyone laughed and told her to quit playing lol. Months later she was diagnosed with a astrocytoma and needed emergency surgery. After surgery she developed meningitis, and had to learn to walk and talk again. The entire tumor couldn't be removed because part of it is attached to her brain stem. So she has regular scans to check for growth and has been back in surgery to remove what they can twice more. She also has a shunt now. She's 26 now, married, a nurse, with three boys. And it's crazy, but less than a year later I was also diagnosed with a brain tumor in 2012. Totally unrelated, just a crazy coincidence

Is it possible to have an article, obituary, discussion, news segment etc., about cancer without the associated concept of it being a "battle"? I have two, stage four, terminal cancers. I'm not special, unique, better, worse, wiser, above or below any other human being. It is not a "battle." One experiences breathtaking physical pain, certainly. It is, overwhelmingly, an extraordinarily beautiful gift (as is EACH moment of everyone's life, without exception), an opportunity for greater understanding (and yes, even joy) of our miraculous lives (if one chooses to see it that way). I would never desire that anyone experience it, however.

This story really touched my heart because it hits home personally. I cried through the whole video and still crying as I am typing. My brother, although not as young as Isabella (heâ€™s 40) late summer, early Fall 2023 started complaining of problems with his hip. He went to his family doctor only to be told that he had a hip sprain, given some pain medication to take, but no testing was done. The pain temporarily went away but quickly reoccurred. He went back to the doctor and asked the doctor if it was something else going on and the doctor at that point decided to order an MRI not right away but sometime in January 2024. My sister came home to take my nephew to a follow up appointment at Duke on Dec. 18, 2023 so that I wouldnâ€™t have to miss another day out of work because 1 year ago today, he lost his mother (our oldest sister) in death. When they returned, my sister noticed that my brothers left leg was swollen, she told him that wasnâ€™t normal and that she was taking him to the ER. He was there in the local hospital all night and most of Tuesday, Dec. 19th until about 3:30 pm when ECU Health finally came to transport him to their hospital. After arriving, they immediately began their own testing, from Ultrasounds, to CT scans, and an MRI. We are thankful that his MRI came back good, but unfortunately, he was diagnosed with late stage 3 early stage 4 B-Cell Lymphoma Cancer. He has a mass almost 4 inches big on his left side in his pelvic area which has blocked the blood & fluid flow from his upper body to his lower body thus causing the swelling. The cancer has eaten away part of his pelvic bone which was causing the pain in what he thought initially was hip pain. In addition, the CT scan showed a tumor under each arm, 1 in his chest, and 1 in his back. He has finished up his 1st round of chemotherapy and will be starting the 2nd round of treatment this coming Thursday. Right now, heâ€™s bedridden due to the swelling in his leg and the deteriorated pelvic bone because the doctors donâ€™t want him putting pressure on his left side because he risk the chance of falling and breaking the bone as well as his hip. After 3 - 4 rounds of chemotherapy treatment, another CT scan will be done to see what the cancer looks like (hoping & praying that it will be gone). If the cancer cells are gone, he will have 2 more rounds of treatment and begin talking with the orthopedic doctor to determine next steps as it pertains to repairing his pelvic bone. I am a parent of a child who had medulloblastoma at the age of 9. She was diagnosed just a day or two before her 9th birthday. I know how it feels to be that parent that doesn't know what to do or how to do it but you learn. One thing he said is that he learned that you are not as strong as you think you are, I have to disagree with that because I found that I was stronger than I thought I was and also because you have to be strong.   That strength comes out of no where because your child needs you, your children need you. You have to be there for the child that is going thru it but you also have to be there for the child or children that is watching their sibling go thru this and for the child or children that feels neglected. (I know this because my daughter always told me she felt neglected even though I did everything I could to be there for her too).  Watching this segment on Isabella made me think about the things that my daughter went through and it was exactly as Isabella where she had to learn how to walk again. It is very painful having to see your child go thru this.  Sadly my daughter died January 31, 2021 from a different cancer (Glioblastoma Multiforme) at the age of 21.  I am praying for Isabella and her family. Cancer affects her body, her mind and her spirit, but it also affects the family because everything  she goes through they watch her go thru it and hurt for her.   May God continue to bless their family!
